## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the right-hand side of a population dynamics ODE. Classical models include density-dependent growth (logistic, Gompertz, theta-logistic) and potentially time-varying parameters.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect with minimum viable population)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 - c2 * P) (per-capita growth rate increases then decreases with P)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (growth with contest competition)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * (c3 + c4 * P) (generalized growth with flexible inflection)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (logistic with seasonal forcing)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (cubic growth model with multiple equilibria)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (logistic growth with saturating harvest)
- Exponential decay carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (time-dependent carrying capacity)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic-catabolic balance model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P → fundamental self-replication dynamics, dP/dt ~ c*P appears in nearly all population models
- Quadratic term P² with negative coefficient → intraspecific competition / density-dependent mortality limiting growth
- Cubic terms in P → multiple equilibria or bistability (e.g., Allee effect with both extinction and carrying capacity equilibria)
- Product P*(1 - c*P) structure → logistic-type self-limiting growth with a single stable carrying capacity
- Logarithmic coupling log(P) → Gompertz-type dynamics where per-capita growth rate declines logarithmically
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) → periodic environmental forcing (seasonal reproduction or resource availability)
- Ratio P/(P+c) → saturating functional response (Type II), common in harvesting or predation terms
- Product P*(P-c1)*(c2-P) → strong Allee effect with unstable lower threshold and stable upper equilibrium
- Exponential time factor exp(c*t) → exponentially changing environmental conditions or resource depletion
- Fractional power P**c with 0<c<1 → sub-linear growth suggesting surface-area-limited or diffusion-limited processes

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and determine if any candidate can match it.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.17*(−1 + P/1.047)*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − exp(−0.097*P))*P
```

Let me expand this carefully.

**First term:** 0.17*(−1 + P/1.047)*(1 − P/10.21)*P
= 0.17*(P/1.047 − 1)*(1 − P/10.21)*P

Let me expand (P/1.047 − 1)*(1 − P/10.21):
= P/1.047 − P²/(1.047·10.21) − 1 + P/10.21
= −P²/10.69 + P/1.047 + P/10.21 − 1
= −P²/10.69 + P·(1/1.047 + 1/10.21) − 1

Multiplying by 0.17·P:
= 0.17·(−P³/10.69 + P²·(1/1.047 + 1/10.21) − P)

**Second term:** 0.17*(1 − P/10.21)*P = 0.17·P − 0.17·P²/10.21

**Third term:** 0.17*(1 − exp(−0.097·P))*P = 0.17·P − 0.17·P·exp(−0.097·P)

Combining all terms:
- **P³ term:** −0.17/10.69 ≈ −0.0159
- **P² term:** 0.17·(1/1.047 + 1/10.21) − 0.17/10.21 = 0.17/1.047 ≈ 0.1624
- **P term:** −0.17 + 0.17 + 0.17 = 0.17
- **Exponential term:** −0.17·P·exp(−0.097·P)

So GT ≈ −0.0159·P³ + 0.1624·P² + 0.17·P − 0.17·P·exp(−0.097·P)

The GT has the form: **c₀·P³ + c₁·P² + c₂·P + c₃·P·exp(c₄·P)** where c₄ < 0.

Now I need to find candidates that can produce: P³ polynomial + P² polynomial + P linear + P·exp(negative·P).

Note that exp(c·P) with c < 0 can be written as exp(c·P).

Let me check candidates with both polynomial and exponential terms:

**Candidate 21:** P³·c0 + P²·c1 + c2·exp(P·c3) + c4·cos(c5·exp(P·c6))
This has exp(P·c3) but not P·exp(...). No direct P·exp term. ❌

**Candidate 68:** P³·c0 + P²·c1 + P·c2 + c3·exp(P·c4) + c5·(P·c6+1)³
Expanding (P·c6+1)³ = c6³·P³ + 3c6²·P² + 3c6·P + 1
This gives: polynomial in P (up to P³) + c3·exp(P·c4). But GT needs P·exp(P·c), not just exp(P·c). ❌

**Candidate 20:** P³·c0 + P²·c1 + P·c2 + c3 + c4·log(c5·exp(P·c6) + 1)
When c5·exp(P·c6) >> 1 (for large P with c6 > 0), log ≈ P·c6 + log(c5), which is linear. But for c6 < 0, when P large, log(c5·exp(c6·P)+1) ≈ log(1) = 0. This doesn't reproduce P·exp(c·P). ❌

**Candidate 58:** P²·c0 + P·c1 + c2·exp(P·c3) + c4·log(c5·exp(P·c6)+1)
Similar issue - can't produce P·exp(c·P). ❌

After checking all candidates systematically, none can produce the **P·exp(c·P)** term that appears in the GT. The candidates either have exp(P·c) (without the P multiplier), log-based terms, trigonometric terms, or power-law terms P^c, none of which can replicate P·exp(c·P).

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG9)

GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P

Matched candidates: []

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
0.17*(P/1.047 - 1)*(1 - P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 - P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 - exp(-0.097*P))*P
```

Let me expand this:

**Term 1:** `0.17*(P/1.047 - 1)*(1 - P/10.21)*P`
= 0.17*(P/1.047 - 1)*(1 - P/10.21)*P

Let me denote a = 1/1.047 ≈ 0.955, b = 1/10.21 ≈ 0.098, k = 0.17, d = 0.097

Term 1: k*(aP - 1)*(1 - bP)*P = k*(aP - abP² - 1 + bP)*P = k*(a+b)P² - k*ab*P³ - k*P + k*bP²... wait let me be more careful.

(aP - 1)(1 - bP) = aP - abP² - 1 + bP = (a+b)P - abP² - 1

So Term 1 = k*[(a+b)P² - abP³ - P]

**Term 2:** k*(1 - bP)*P = k*P - k*b*P²

**Term 3:** k*(1 - exp(-dP))*P = k*P - k*exp(-dP)*P

Combining Terms 1+2+3:
= k*(a+b)P² - k*ab*P³ - k*P + k*P - k*b*P² + k*P - k*exp(-dP)*P
= -k*ab*P³ + k*(a+b-b)P² + k*P - k*P*exp(-dP)
= -k*ab*P³ + k*a*P² + k*P - k*P*exp(-dP)
= -k*ab*P³ + k*a*P² + k*P*(1 - exp(-dP))

With numerical values:
- k*ab = 0.17 * (1/1.047) * (1/10.21) ≈ 0.17 * 0.0935 ≈ 0.0159
- k*a = 0.17 * 0.955 ≈ 0.1623
- k = 0.17
- d = 0.097

So GT = **c₁*P³ + c₂*P² + c₃*P - c₃*P*exp(-d*P)**

where c₁ < 0, c₂ > 0, c₃ > 0, d > 0.

The key basis functions are: **P³, P², P, P*exp(-dP)** (where d > 0, so exp(-dP) is a decaying exponential).

Note: P*exp(-dP) with d > 0 means this involves exp(negative * P).

Now let me check each candidate for structural compatibility.

The GT has these basis functions:
1. P³
2. P²  
3. P
4. P·exp(-dP) where d > 0

### Candidate 16: P²c₀ + Pc₁ + c₂·exp(Pc₃) + c₄·(Pc₅+1)³ + c₆·exp(P²c₇)
Expand (Pc₅+1)³ = c₅³P³ + 3c₅²P² + 3c₅P + 1. So this gives:
P²c₀ + Pc₁ + c₂·exp(Pc₃) + c₄c₅³P³ + 3c₄c₅²P² + 3c₄c₅P + c₄ + c₆·exp(P²c₇)

Unless... the constant is small enough? No, we need exact match. The GT has no constant term (at P=0, GT=0). But this candidate at P=0 gives c₄ + c₂ ≠ 0 in general. We'd need c₄ + c₂ = 0, so c₂ = -c₄. Then exp term becomes -c₄·exp(Pc₃). At P=0 this gives -c₄, canceling c₄. But then the full expression is c₄c₅³P³ + (c₀+3c₄c₅²)P² + (c₁+3c₄c₅)P + c₄(1-exp(Pc₃)). 

GT = αP³ + βP² + γP - γP·exp(-dP) = αP³ + βP² + γP(1 - exp(-dP))

Candidate (with c₂=-c₄, c₆=0): αP³ + βP² + δP + c₄(1-exp(Pc₃))

The GT has γP(1-exp(-dP)) = γP - γP·exp(-dP), while candidate has δP + c₄(1-exp(Pc₃)) = δP + c₄ - c₄·exp(Pc₃).

For these to match: c₄(1-exp(Pc₃)) should equal γP(1-exp(-dP)). But c₄ is a constant while γP is linear in P. These can't be equal for all P. Cannot match.
Candidate 16 verdict: [NO MATCH]

## Summary

The GT has basis functions {P³, P², P, P·exp(-dP)}. None of the candidates have the P·exp(cP) basis function. Many have exp(cP) (without the P multiplier), log terms, sin terms, or other incompatible structures. The key distinguishing feature is that the GT requires a **P·exp(cP)** term, which none of the candidates provide.
